Playoff</a>)\n</p>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_NCAA_Division_I_FBS_football_programs" title="List of NCAA Division I FBS football programs">List of NCAA Division I FBS football programs</a></div>\n<dl><dt>Notes</dt></dl>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap mw-references-columns"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-92"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-92">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The conference was founded in 1979 as the <a href="/wiki/Big_East_Conference_(1979%E2%80%932013)" title="Big East Conference (1979\xe2\x80\x932013)">original Big East Conference</a>. It renamed itself the American Athletic Conference following a <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9313_Big_East_Conference_realignment" title="2010\xe2\x80\x9313 Big East Conference realignment">2013 split</a> along football lines. The non-FBS schools of the original conference left to form a new conference that purchased <a href="/wiki/Big_East_Conference" title="Big East Conference">the Big East name</a>, while the FBS schools continued to operate under the old Big East\'s charter and structure. The American also inherited the old Big East\'s <a href="/wiki/Bowl_Championship_Series" title="Bowl Championship Series">Bowl Championship Series</a> berth for the 2013 season, the last for the BCS.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-93"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-93">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">11 of the 12 full members sponsor football, with <a href="/wiki/Wichita_State_University" title="Wichita State University">Wichita State</a> as the only non-football member.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-94"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-94">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In addition to the full members, six schools have single-sport associate membership:\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/United_States_Naval_Academy" title="United States Naval Academy">Navy</a> is a football-only member.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Florida" title="University of Florida">Florida</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vanderbilt_University" title="Vanderbilt University">Vanderbilt</a> are members in women\'s lacrosse.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Old_Dominion_University" title="Old Dominion University">Old Dominion</a>, <a href="/wiki/California_State_University,_Sacramento" title="California State University, Sacramento">Sacramento State</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_State_University" title="San Diego State University">San Diego State</a> are members in women\'s rowing.</li></ul>\n</span></li>\n<li id="cite_note-95"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-95">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/University_of_Notre_Dame" title="University of Notre Dame">Notre Dame</a> is a full member except in football, in which it remains independent. It has committed to play five games each season against ACC opponents, and to play each other ACC member at least once every three years.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-96"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-96">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In addition to the full members, two schools have affiliate membership:\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_University" title="Johns Hopkins University">Johns Hopkins</a>, otherwise a <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_III" title="NCAA Division III">Division III</a> member, is an affiliate in both <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_Blue_Jays_men%27s_lacrosse" title="Johns Hopkins Blue Jays men&#39;s lacrosse">men\'s</a> and <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_Blue_Jays_women%27s_lacrosse" title="Johns Hopkins Blue Jays women&#39;s lacrosse">women\'s</a> lacrosse, sports in which the school fields Division I teams.</li>\n<li>Notre Dame is a men\'s hockey affiliate.</li></ul>\n</span></li>\n<li id="cite_note-97"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-97">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In addition to the full members, the Big 12 has 11 members that participate in only one sport:\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/United_States_Air_Force_Academy" title="United States Air Force Academy">Air Force</a>, <a href="/wiki/California_State_University,_Fresno" title="California State University, Fresno">Fresno State</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Dakota_State_University" title="North Dakota State University">North Dakota State</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Northern_Colorado" title="University of Northern Colorado">Northern Colorado</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Northern_Iowa" title="University of Northern Iowa">Northern Iowa</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Dakota_State_University" title="South Dakota State University">South Dakota State</a>, <a href="/wiki/Utah_Valley_University" title="Utah Valley University">Utah Valley</a>, and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Wyoming" title="University of Wyoming">Wyoming</a> in wrestling.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Alabama" title="University of Alabama">Alabama</a> and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Tennessee" title="University of Tennessee">Tennessee</a> in women\'s rowing.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Denver" title="University of Denver">Denver</a> in women\'s gymnastics.</li></ul>\n</span></li>\n<li id="cite_note-98"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-98">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The conference was founded in 1995, with football competition starting in 1996.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-99"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-99">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In addition to the 14 full members, Conference USA features three schools that play <a href="/wiki/College_soccer" title="College soccer">men\'s soccer</a> in the conference: <a href="/wiki/University_of_Kentucky" title="University of Kentucky">Kentucky</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_New_Mexico" title="University of New Mexico">New Mexico</a>, and <a href="/wiki/University_of_South_Carolina" title="University of South Carolina">South Carolina</a>. New Mexico will drop men\'s soccer after the 2018 season.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-100"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-100">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Note that "Independents" is not a conference; it is simply a designation used for schools whose football programs do not play in any conference. All of these schools have conference memberships for other sports.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-101"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-101">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In addition to the 12 full members, the Mid-American Conference features nine members which only participate in one sport each, plus one other school that competes in two sports.\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Appalachian_State_University" title="Appalachian State University">Appalachian State</a> and <a href="/wiki/Longwood_University" title="Longwood University">Longwood</a> compete in <a href="/wiki/Field_hockey" title="Field hockey">women\'s field hockey</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Binghamton_University" title="Binghamton University">Binghamton</a> competes in men\'s tennis.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Evansville" title="University of Evansville">Evansville</a>, <a href="/wiki/Missouri_State_University" title="Missouri State University">Missouri State</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Southern_Illinois_University_Carbondale" title="Southern Illinois University Carbondale">Southern Illinois</a> compete in men\'s swimming and diving.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Missouri" title="University of Missouri">Missouri</a> and <a href="/wiki/Old_Dominion_University" title="Old Dominion University">Old Dominion</a> compete in <a href="/wiki/Collegiate_wrestling" title="Collegiate wrestling">wrestling</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/West_Virginia_University" title="West Virginia University">West Virginia</a> competes in men\'s soccer.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Southern_Illinois_University_Edwardsville" title="Southern Illinois University Edwardsville">SIU Edwardsville</a> competes in men\'s soccer and wrestling.</li></ul>\n</span></li>\n<li id="cite_note-102"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-102">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Since 2012, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Hawaii_at_Manoa" title="University of Hawaii at Manoa">Hawai\xca\xbbi</a> has been a football-only associate member, with most of its remaining teams in the non-football <a href="/wiki/Big_West_Conference" title="Big West Conference">Big West Conference</a>.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-103"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-103">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In addition to the 11 full members and football affiliate Hawai\xca\xbbi, <a href="/wiki/Colorado_College" title="Colorado College">Colorado College</a>, a Division III school with a Division I <a href="/wiki/Colorado_College_Tigers_men%27s_ice_hockey" title="Colorado College Tigers men&#39;s ice hockey">men\'s ice hockey team</a>, plays Division I women\'s soccer in the MW.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-104"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-104">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The charter of the Pac-12 dates only to the formation of the Athletic Association of Western Universities (AAWU) in 1959. However, the Pac-12 claims the history of the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Coast_Conference" title="Pacific Coast Conference">Pacific Coast Conference</a>, which was founded in 1915 and began competition in 1916, as its own. Of the nine members of the PCC at the time of its demise in June 1959, only <a href="/wiki/University_of_Idaho" title="University of Idaho">Idaho</a> never joined the Pac-12. The PCC\'s berth in the <a href="/wiki/Rose_Bowl_Game" title="Rose Bowl Game">Rose Bowl</a> passed to the AAWU.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-105"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-105">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Pac-12 also includes several associate members which compete in one or two sports in the conference. <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_State_University" title="San Diego State University">San Diego State</a> plays men\'s soccer. <a href="/wiki/California_State_University,_Bakersfield" title="California State University, Bakersfield">Cal State Bakersfield</a> and <a href="/wiki/California_Polytechnic_State_University" title="California Polytechnic State University">Cal Poly</a> compete in <a href="/wiki/Collegiate_wrestling" title="Collegiate wrestling">wrestling</a>. Cal Poly also participates in men\'s <a href="/wiki/Swimming_(sport)" title="Swimming (sport)">swimming</a> and <a href="/wiki/Diving" title="Diving">diving</a>, which the NCAA considers a single sport. <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Santa_Barbara" title="University of California, Santa Barbara">UC Santa Barbara</a> only competes in men\'s swimming and diving.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-106"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-106">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Ten Sun Belt Conference members currently sponsor football, with <a href="/wiki/University_of_Arkansas_at_Little_Rock" title="University of Arkansas at Little Rock">Little Rock</a> and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Texas_at_Arlington" title="University of Texas at Arlington">UT Arlington</a> as members that do not play football at all.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-107"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-107">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Howard_University" title="Howard University">Howard</a> is a men\'s soccer affiliate. <a href="/wiki/University_of_Central_Arkansas" title="University of Central Arkansas">Central Arkansas</a> will become a men\'s soccer affiliate in 2019.</span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Football_Championship_Subdivision">Football Championship Subdivision</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=NCAA_Division_I&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Football Championship Subdivision">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I_Football_Championship" title="NCAA Division I Football Championship">NCAA Division I Football Championship</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_NCAA_Division_I_FCS_football_programs" title="List of NCAA Division I FCS football programs">List of NCAA Division I FCS football programs</a></div>\n<p>The <b>Division I Football Championship Subdivision</b> (<b>FCS</b>), formerly known as <b>Division I-AA</b>, determines its national champion through a <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I_Football_Championship" title="NCAA Division I Football Championship">24-team, single-elimination tournament</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> With the expansion of the tournament field in 2013 from 20 teams to 24, the champions of 11 conferences receive automatic bids, with 13 "at-large" spots; and the top 8 teams receive first-round byes. A team must have at least seven wins to be eligible for an at-large spot.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The tournament traditionally begins on <a href="/wiki/Thanksgiving_(United_States)" title="Thanksgiving (United States)">Thanksgiving</a> weekend in late November, and during the era of the 16-team field ran for four weeks, ending with the championship game in mid-December. Since 2010, the tournament has run for four weeks (for seeds 9\xe2\x80\x9324) to determine the two finalists, who play for the FCS national title in early January in <a href="/wiki/Frisco,_Texas" title="Frisco, Texas">Frisco, Texas</a>, the scheduled host through the 2019 season. For thirteen seasons, the title game was played in <a href="/wiki/Chattanooga,_Tennessee" title="Chattanooga, Tennessee">Chattanooga, Tennessee</a>, (1997\xe2\x80\x932009), preceded by five seasons in <a href="/wiki/Huntington,_West_Virginia" title="Huntington, West Virginia">Huntington, West Virginia</a>, where host <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Thundering_Herd_football" title="Marshall Thundering Herd football">Marshall</a> advanced to the title game in four of the five years.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>When I-AA was formed 40 years ago in <a href="/wiki/1978_NCAA_Division_I-AA_football_season" title="1978 NCAA Division I-AA football season">1978</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-bswb_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bswb-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> the playoffs included just four teams for its first three seasons, doubling to eight teams for one season in <a href="/wiki/1981_NCAA_Division_I-AA_football_season#Postseason" title="1981 NCAA Division I-AA football season">1981</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-nexeig_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nexeig-112">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> From <a href="/wiki/1982_NCAA_Division_I-AA_football_season#Postseason" title="1982 NCAA Division I-AA football season">1982</a> to <a href="/wiki/1985_NCAA_Division_I-AA_football_season#Postseason" title="1985 NCAA Division I-AA football season">1985</a>, I-AA had a 12-team tournament, with each of the top four seeds receiving a first-round bye and a home game in the quarterfinals.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> The I-AA playoffs went to 16 teams in <a href="/wiki/1986_NCAA_Division_I-AA_football_season#Postseason" title="1986 NCAA Division I-AA football season">1986</a>, and the FCS playoffs expanded to 20 teams starting in <a href="/wiki/2010_NCAA_Division_I_FCS_football_season" title="2010 NCAA Division I FCS football season">2010</a> and to 24 in 2013. After 28 seasons, the "I-AA" was dropped by the NCAA twelve years ago in <a href="/wiki/2006_NCAA_Division_I_FCS_football_season" title="2006 NCAA Division I FCS football season">2006</a>, although it is still informally and commonly used.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Abstainers">Abstainers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=NCAA_Division_I&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Abstainers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Football Championship Subdivision includes several conferences which do not participate in the eponymous post-season championship tournament.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Ivy_League" title="Ivy League">Ivy League</a> was reclassified to I-AA (FCS) following the <a href="/wiki/1981_NCAA_Division_I-A_football_season" title="1981 NCAA Division I-A football season">1981 season</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> and plays a strict ten-game schedule. Although it qualifies for an automatic bid, the Ivy League has not played any postseason games at all since becoming a conference for the <a href="/wiki/1956_college_football_season" title="1956 college football season">1956 college football season</a>, citing academic concerns. (The last college which is now an Ivy League member to play in a bowl game was <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Lions_football" title="Columbia Lions football">Columbia</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1934_Rose_Bowl" title="1934 Rose Bowl">1934 Rose Bowl</a>.)\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Southwestern_Athletic_Conference" title="Southwestern Athletic Conference">Southwestern Athletic Conference</a> (SWAC) has its own <a href="/wiki/SWAC_Championship_Game" title="SWAC Championship Game">championship game</a> in mid-December between the champions of its East and West divisions. Also, three of its member schools traditionally do not finish their regular seasons until Thanksgiving weekend. <a href="/wiki/Grambling_State_Tigers_football" title="Grambling State Tigers football">Grambling State</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southern_Jaguars_football" title="Southern Jaguars football">Southern</a> play each other in the <a href="/wiki/Bayou_Classic" title="Bayou Classic">Bayou Classic</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Alabama_State_Hornets_football" title="Alabama State Hornets football">Alabama State</a> plays <a href="/wiki/Tuskegee_Golden_Tigers_football" title="Tuskegee Golden Tigers football">Tuskegee</a> (of <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_II" title="NCAA Division II">Division II</a>) in the Turkey Day Classic. SWAC teams are eligible to accept at-large bids if their schedule is not in conflict. The last SWAC team to participate in the I-AA playoffs was <a href="/wiki/Jackson_State_Tigers_football" title="Jackson State Tigers football">Jackson State</a> in <a href="/wiki/1997_NCAA_Division_I-AA_football_season#Postseason" title="1997 NCAA Division I-AA football season">1997</a>; the SWAC never achieved success in the tournament, going winless in 19 games in twenty years (1978\xe2\x80\x9397). It had greater success outside the conference while in Division II and the preceding College Division.\n</p><p>From 2006 through 2009, the <a href="/wiki/Pioneer_Football_League" title="Pioneer Football League">Pioneer Football League</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Conference" title="Northeast Conference">Northeast Conference</a> champions played in the <a href="/wiki/Gridiron_Classic_(2006%E2%80%932009)" title="Gridiron Classic (2006\xe2\x80\x932009)">Gridiron Classic</a>. If a league champion was invited to the national championship playoff as an at-large bid (something the Pioneer league, at least, never received), the second-place team would play in the Gridiron Classic. That game was scrapped after the 2009 season when its four-year contract ran out; this coincided with the NCAA\'s announcement that the Northeast Conference would get an automatic bid to the tournament starting in 2010. The <a href="/wiki/Big_South_Conference" title="Big South Conference">Big South Conference</a> also received an automatic bid in the same season. The Pioneer Football League earned an automatic bid beginning in 2013.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Mid-Eastern_Athletic_Conference" title="Mid-Eastern Athletic Conference">Mid-Eastern Athletic Conference</a> (MEAC) began abstaining from the playoffs with the 2015 season. Like the SWAC, its members are eligible for at-large bids, and the two conferences have faced off in the <a href="/wiki/Celebration_Bowl" title="Celebration Bowl">Celebration Bowl</a> as an alternative postseason game since the 2015 season.\n</p><p>Schools in a transition period after joining the FCS from a lower division (or from the <a href="/wiki/National_Association_of_Intercollegiate_Athletics" title="National Association of Intercollegiate Athletics">NAIA</a>) are also ineligible for the playoffs.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Scholarships">Scholarships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=NCAA_Division_I&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Scholarships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Division I FCS schools are currently restricted to giving financial assistance amounting to 63 full scholarships. As FCS football is an "equivalency" sport (as opposed to the "head-count" status of FBS football), Championship Subdivision schools may divide their allotment into partial scholarships. However, FCS schools may only have 85 players receiving any sort of athletic financial aid for football\xe2\x80\x94the same numeric limit as FBS schools. Because of competitive forces, however, a substantial number of players in Championship Subdivision programs are on full scholarships. Another difference is that FCS schools no longer have a limit on the number of new players that can be provided with financial aid in a given season, while FBS schools are limited to 25 such additions per season. Finally, FCS schools are limited to 95 individuals participating in preseason practices, as opposed to 105 at FBS schools (the three service academies that play FBS football are exempt from preseason practice player limits by NCAA rule).\n</p><p>A few Championship Subdivision conferences are composed of schools that offer no athletic scholarships at all, most notably the <a href="/wiki/Ivy_League" title="Ivy League">Ivy League</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Pioneer_Football_League" title="Pioneer Football League">Pioneer Football League</a> (PFL), a football-only conference. The Ivy League allows no athletic scholarships at all, while the PFL consists of schools that offer scholarships in other sports but choose not to take on the expense of a scholarship football program. The <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Conference" title="Northeast Conference">Northeast Conference</a> also sponsored non-scholarship football, but began offering a maximum of 30 full scholarship equivalents in 2006, which grew to 40 in 2011 after a later vote of the league\'s school presidents and athletic directors. The <a href="/wiki/Patriot_League" title="Patriot League">Patriot League</a> only began awarding football scholarships in the 2013 season, with the first scholarships awarded only to incoming freshmen. Before the conference began its transition to scholarship football, athletes receiving scholarships in other sports were ineligible to play football for member schools. Since the completion of the transition with the 2016 season, member schools have been allowed up to 60 full scholarship equivalents.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Conferences_3">Conferences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=NCAA_Division_I&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Conferences">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="wikitable title="List of NCAA Division I FCS football programs">List of NCAA Division I FCS football programs</a></div>\n<dl><dt>Notes</dt></dl>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap mw-references-columns"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-116"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-116">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">13 football members with <a href="/wiki/Cal_Poly_Mustangs_football" title="Cal Poly Mustangs football">Cal Poly</a> and <a href="/wiki/UC_Davis_Aggies_football" title="UC Davis Aggies football">UC Davis</a>, both full members of the non-football <a href="/wiki/Big_West_Conference" title="Big West Conference">Big West Conference</a>, as football-only affiliates.\n<ul><li>While <a href="/wiki/University_of_North_Dakota" title="University of North Dakota">North Dakota</a> has become an FCS independent in football, it continues to play a full Big Sky football schedule through the 2019 season, after which it will join the Missouri Valley Football Conference.</li></ul>\n</span></li>\n<li id="cite_note-117"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-117">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In addition to the full members and football affiliates, <a href="/wiki/Binghamton_University" title="Binghamton University">Binghamton</a> and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Hartford" title="University of Hartford">Hartford</a> are associate members in men\'s golf.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-118"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-118">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Big South has four full members that compete for its football championship, plus two football-only associates in <a href="/wiki/Kennesaw_State_Owls_football" title="Kennesaw State Owls football">Kennesaw State</a> and <a href="/wiki/Monmouth_Hawks_football" title="Monmouth Hawks football">Monmouth</a>.\n<ul><li>The following changes are set to take place in the near future:\n<ul><li>In 2019, two additional schools will enter Big South football\xe2\x80\x94<a href="/wiki/Hampton_University" title="Hampton University">Hampton</a>, which joined the league in non-football sports in 2018 and is playing that football season as an FCS independent, and <a href="/wiki/University_of_North_Alabama" title="University of North Alabama">North Alabama</a>, which is spending the first season of its transition from <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_II" title="NCAA Division II">Division II</a> as an FCS independent.</li></ul></li>\n<li>In 2020, Presbyterian football will leave for a transitional season as an FCS independent before joining the Pioneer League. The school will remain a full Big South non-football member.</li></ul>\n</span></li>\n<li id="cite_note-119"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-119">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The CAA football conference was only founded in 2007, but has a continuous history dating to the late 1930s (although not under the same charter):\n<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/New_England_Conference" title="New England Conference">New England Conference</a> was formed by five New England state universities, plus one private university in that region (<a href="/wiki/Northeastern_University" title="Northeastern University">Northeastern</a>), in 1938. Four of the public schools\xe2\x80\x94<a href="/wiki/University_of_Maine" title="University of Maine">Maine</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Massachusetts_Amherst" title="University of Massachusetts Amherst">UMass</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_New_Hampshire" title="University of New Hampshire">New Hampshire</a>, and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Rhode_Island" title="University of Rhode Island">Rhode Island</a>\xe2\x80\x94were in the CAA football conference through the 2011 season. However, <a href="/wiki/UMass_Minutemen_football" title="UMass Minutemen football">UMass football</a> left for the MAC in 2012. <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island_Rams_football" title="Rhode Island Rams football">URI football</a> initially planned to leave for the Northeast Conference in 2013, but decided to remain in the CAA.</li>\n<li>In 1946, the four then-remaining members of the New England Conference affiliated with two other schools to form the <a href="/wiki/Yankee_Conference" title="Yankee Conference">Yankee Conference</a> under a separate charter, with athletic competition starting in 1947.</li>\n<li>In 1997, the Yankee Conference was absorbed by the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_10_Conference" title="Atlantic 10 Conference">Atlantic 10 Conference</a>. The A10 inherited the Yankee Conference\'s automatic berth in the <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I_Football_Championship" title="NCAA Division I Football Championship">Division I-AA (now FCS) playoffs</a>. In addition to the four charter New England Conference members mentioned above, five other members of the Yankee Conference at the time of the A10 merger are still in the CAA football conference.</li>\n<li>After the 2006 season, all of the A10 football teams left for the new CAA football conference. The CAA inherited the A10\'s automatic berth in the FCS playoffs.</li></ul>\n</span></li>\n<li id="cite_note-120"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-120">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The CAA has 10 full members, but only five of them are part of the CAA football conference. Currently, seven associate members fill out the ranks of the CAA football conference: <a href="/wiki/Albany_Great_Danes_football" title="Albany Great Danes football">Albany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maine_Black_Bears_football" title="Maine Black Bears football">Maine</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire_Wildcats_football" title="New Hampshire Wildcats football">New Hampshire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island_Rams_football" title="Rhode Island Rams football">Rhode Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richmond_Spiders_football" title="Richmond Spiders football">Richmond</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stony_Brook_Seawolves_football" title="Stony Brook Seawolves football">Stony Brook</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Villanova_Wildcats_football" title="Villanova Wildcats football">Villanova</a>. Villanova is also a CAA associate in women\'s rowing.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-121"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-121">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In addition to the football associates, the CAA has three other associate members that each participate in one sport:\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Eastern_Michigan_University" title="Eastern Michigan University">Eastern Michigan</a> competes in women\'s rowing.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Fairfield_University" title="Fairfield University">Fairfield</a> and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Massachusetts_Amherst" title="University of Massachusetts Amherst">UMass</a> play men\'s lacrosse.</li></ul>\n</span></li>\n<li id="cite_note-122"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-122">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Note that "Independents" is not a conference; it is simply a designation used for schools whose football programs do not play in any conference. All of these schools have conference memberships for other sports.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-FCSIndy-123"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FCSIndy_123-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">1 independent in 2019 with Hampton and North Alabama joining Big South football.\n<ul><li>1 independent in 2020 with North Dakota joining the MVFC and Presbyterian transitioning to non-scholarship football.</li>\n<li>No independents in 2021 with Presbyterian joining the Pioneer Football League.</li></ul>\n</span></li>\n<li id="cite_note-124"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-124">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Although the conference considers 1954 to be its founding date, the athletic league\'s origins go back to the turn of the 20th century.\n<ul><li>The Ivy League considers the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Intercollegiate_Basketball_League" title="Eastern Intercollegiate Basketball League">Eastern Intercollegiate Basketball League</a> (EIBL), a men\'s basketball-only conference founded in 1901, as part of its history. Every school that had been an EIBL member would become part of the Ivy League.</li>\n<li>In 1945, the eight schools that would eventually form the athletic Ivy League entered into the Ivy Group Agreement, which governed football competition between the schools. The original agreement was renewed in 1952.</li>\n<li>The official founding date of 1954 reflects the extension of the Ivy Group Agreement to all sports. As part of the agreement, <a href="/wiki/Brown_University" title="Brown University">Brown</a>, the only one of the original Ivy Group that had not joined the EIBL, did so. All-sports competition began in 1955, with the EIBL directly absorbed into the new league.</li></ul>\n</span></li>\n<li id="cite_note-125"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-125">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The football conference currently consists of 10 of the 12 member schools.\n<ul><li>11 full members and 9 football members in 2019 with Savannah State dropping to Division II.</li></ul>\n</span></li>\n<li id="cite_note-126"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-126">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In addition to the full members, three other schools are associates in two sports:\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Augusta_University" title="Augusta University">Augusta</a>, a Division II school that operates Division I programs in men\'s and women\'s golf, is an associate member in men\'s golf only.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Monmouth_University" title="Monmouth University">Monmouth</a> and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Alabama_at_Birmingham" title="University of Alabama at Birmingham">UAB</a> participate in women\'s <a href="/wiki/Ten-pin_bowling" title="Ten-pin bowling">bowling</a>.</li></ul>\n</span></li>\n<li id="cite_note-127"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-127">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The football conference dates to 1985, but the conference charter was established in 1982. See <a href="/wiki/Missouri_Valley_Football_Conference#History" title="Missouri Valley Football Conference">History of the Missouri Valley Football Conference</a> for more details.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-128"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-128">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">North Dakota will join the MVFC in 2020.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-129"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-129">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The conference has seven full members that sponsor football. <a href="/wiki/Duquesne_University" title="Duquesne University">Duquesne</a> of the non-football <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_10_Conference" title="Atlantic 10 Conference">Atlantic 10</a> is a football associate.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-130"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-130">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">11 full members, 9 of which sponsor football, with the following changes in 2019:\n<ul><li>Addition of <a href="/wiki/Merrimack_College" title="Merrimack College">Merrimack</a>.</li>\n<li>Merger of the athletic programs of full non-football NEC member <a href="/wiki/LIU_Brooklyn" title="LIU Brooklyn">LIU Brooklyn</a> and Division II football-sponsoring <a href="/wiki/LIU_Post" title="LIU Post">LIU Post</a> into a single athletic program under the LIU name, with the LIU Post football program becoming the new LIU football program.</li></ul>\n</span></li>\n<li id="cite_note-131"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-131">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In addition to Duquesne in football, the NEC has three other associate members that each participate in one sport, with two more single-sport members joining in the near future:\n<ul><li>Division II member <a href="/wiki/Caldwell_University" title="Caldwell University">Caldwell</a> participates in women\'s bowling, as does Duquesne.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hobart_and_William_Smith_Colleges" title="Hobart and William Smith Colleges">Hobart</a>, otherwise a Division III member, and <a href="/wiki/Saint_Joseph%27s_University" title="Saint Joseph&#39;s University">Saint Joseph\'s</a> participate in men\'s lacrosse.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Fairfield_University" title="Fairfield University">Fairfield</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rider_University" title="Rider University">Rider</a> will join for field hockey in 2019.</li></ul>\n</span></li>\n<li id="cite_note-132"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-132">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">23 sports in 2019 with addition of field hockey.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-133"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-133">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The football conference consists of 9 of the 12 member schools. <a href="/wiki/Morehead_State_Eagles_football" title="Morehead State Eagles football">Morehead State</a> plays non-scholarship football in the Pioneer Football League, while <a href="/wiki/Belmont_Bruins" title="Belmont Bruins">Belmont</a> and <a href="/wiki/SIU_Edwardsville_Cougars" title="SIU Edwardsville Cougars">SIU Edwardsville</a> do not sponsor football.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-134"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-134">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Patriot League was founded as the football-only Colonial League in 1986. In 1990, it became an all-sports conference and adopted its current name.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-135"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-135">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Five of the full members do not sponsor FCS football. <a href="/wiki/American_University" title="American University">American</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boston_University" title="Boston University">Boston University</a> and <a href="/wiki/Loyola_University_Maryland" title="Loyola University Maryland">Loyola (Maryland)</a> do not sponsor football at all; <a href="/wiki/United_States_Military_Academy" title="United States Military Academy">Army</a> is an <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I_FBS_independent_schools" title="NCAA Division I FBS independent schools">FBS independent</a>; and <a href="/wiki/United_States_Naval_Academy" title="United States Naval Academy">Navy</a> plays in the <a href="/wiki/American_Athletic_Conference" title="American Athletic Conference">American Athletic Conference</a>. <a href="/wiki/Fordham_University" title="Fordham University">Fordham</a> and <a href="/wiki/Georgetown_University" title="Georgetown University">Georgetown</a> are associate members in football.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-136"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-136">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In addition to the football associates, two other schools have single-sport membership:\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology" title="Massachusetts Institute of Technology">MIT</a>, otherwise a Division III institution, is an associate in women\'s rowing.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Richmond" title="University of Richmond">Richmond</a> is a women\'s golf associate.</li></ul>\n</span></li>\n<li id="cite_note-137"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-137">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">11 members in 2021 with arrival of Presbyterian.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-138"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-138">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In addition to the full members, the SoCon currently has 16 associate members which play one sport in the conference, with one more school set to become an associate in the near future:\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/United_States_Air_Force_Academy" title="United States Air Force Academy">Air Force</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bellarmine_University" title="Bellarmine University">Bellarmine</a> (a Division II institution that sponsors Division I men\'s lacrosse), <a href="/wiki/High_Point_University" title="High Point University">High Point</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_University" title="Jacksonville University">Jacksonville</a>, and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Richmond" title="University of Richmond">Richmond</a> are members in men\'s lacrosse. Jacksonville is a full member of the Atlantic Sun Conference, which has a formal relationship with the SoCon in men\'s lacrosse. The newest ASUN member, <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Institute_of_Technology" title="New Jersey Institute of Technology">NJIT</a>, sponsors men\'s lacrosse, but did not immediately join in men\'s lacrosse; no official announcement has yet been made regarding when that team will join.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Appalachian_State_University" title="Appalachian State University">Appalachian State</a>, <a href="/wiki/Campbell_University" title="Campbell University">Campbell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Davidson_College" title="Davidson College">Davidson</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gardner%E2%80%93Webb_University" title="Gardner\xe2\x80\x93Webb University">Gardner\xe2\x80\x93Webb</a> are members in <a href="/wiki/Collegiate_wrestling" title="Collegiate wrestling">wrestling</a>. <a href="/wiki/Presbyterian_College" title="Presbyterian College">Presbyterian</a> will join this group of schools in 2019.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Central_Michigan_University" title="Central Michigan University">Central Michigan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delaware_State_University" title="Delaware State University">Delaware State</a>, and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Detroit_Mercy" title="University of Detroit Mercy">Detroit Mercy</a> are members in women\'s lacrosse.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Georgia_Southern_University" title="Georgia Southern University">Georgia Southern</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_North_Georgia" title="University of North Georgia">North Georgia</a> (a Division II institution), and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Alabama_at_Birmingham" title="University of Alabama at Birmingham">UAB</a> are members in rifle. Rifle has <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Rifle_Championship" title="NCAA Rifle Championship">a single national championship</a> for all divisions.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Belmont_University" title="Belmont University">Belmont</a> is a member in men\'s soccer.</li></ul>\n</span></li>\n<li id="cite_note-139"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-139">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The football conference currently consists of 11 of the 13 member schools.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-140"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-140">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In addition to the full members, <a href="/wiki/Howard_University" title="Howard University">Howard</a> is an associate member in women\'s soccer.</span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Division_I_non-football_schools">Division I non-football schools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=NCAA_Division_I&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Division I non-football schools">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Several Bowl Subdivision and Championship Subdivision conferences have member institutions that do not compete in football. Such schools are sometimes unofficially referred to as I-AAA.<sup id="cite_ref-Division_IAAA_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Division_IAAA-141">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The following non-football conferences have full members that sponsor football:\n</p>\n<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/America_East_Conference" title="America East Conference">America East Conference</a> has four football-sponsoring schools, all of which play in the <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Athletic_Association" title="Colonial Athletic Association">Colonial Athletic Association</a> (CAA)\xe2\x80\x94<a href="/wiki/University_at_Albany,_SUNY" title="University at Albany, SUNY">Albany</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Maine" title="University of Maine">Maine</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_New_Hampshire" title="University of New Hampshire">New Hampshire</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Stony_Brook_University" title="Stony Brook University">Stony Brook</a>.</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Sun_Conference" title="Atlantic Sun Conference">Atlantic Sun Conference</a> (ASUN) has five football-sponsoring members:\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_University" title="Jacksonville University">Jacksonville</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stetson_University" title="Stetson University">Stetson</a> play in the <a href="/wiki/Pioneer_Football_League" title="Pioneer Football League">Pioneer Football League</a> (PFL).</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Kennesaw_State_University" title="Kennesaw State University">Kennesaw State</a> plays in the <a href="/wiki/Big_South_Conference" title="Big South Conference">Big South Conference</a>. <a href="/wiki/University_of_North_Alabama" title="University of North Alabama">North Alabama</a>, which joined in 2018 from <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_II" title="NCAA Division II">NCAA Division II</a>, will spend the first year of its D-I transition as an FCS independent in 2018 before becoming a football-only Big South member in 2019.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Liberty_University" title="Liberty University">Liberty</a>, which also joined the ASUN in 2018, is currently transitioning from FCS to FBS; it is classified as an FBS independent for scheduling purposes in 2018 before gaining full FBS membership in 2019.</li></ul></li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_10_Conference" title="Atlantic 10 Conference">Atlantic 10 Conference</a> has seven football-sponsoring members:\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Davidson_Wildcats_football" title="Davidson Wildcats football">Davidson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dayton_Flyers_football" title="Dayton Flyers football">Dayton</a> play in the PFL.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Duquesne_Dukes_football" title="Duquesne Dukes football">Duquesne</a> plays in the <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Conference" title="Northeast Conference">Northeast Conference</a> (NEC).</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Fordham_Rams_football" title="Fordham Rams football">Fordham</a> plays in the <a href="/wiki/Patriot_League" title="Patriot League">Patriot League</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island_Rams_football" title="Rhode Island Rams football">Rhode Island</a> and <a href="/wiki/Richmond_Spiders_football" title="Richmond Spiders football">Richmond</a> play in the CAA.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/UMass_Minutemen_football" title="UMass Minutemen football">UMass</a> plays FBS football as an Independent.</li></ul></li>\n<li>The current <a href="/wiki/Big_East_Conference" title="Big East Conference">Big East Conference</a> has three football-sponsoring schools, all of which play in FCS\xe2\x80\x94<a href="/wiki/Butler_Bulldogs_football" title="Butler Bulldogs football">Butler</a> in the PFL, <a href="/wiki/Georgetown_Hoyas_football" title="Georgetown Hoyas football">Georgetown</a> in the Patriot League, and <a href="/wiki/Villanova_Wildcats_football" title="Villanova Wildcats football">Villanova</a> in the CAA.</li>\n<li>Three <a href="/wiki/Big_West_Conference" title="Big West Conference">Big West Conference</a> members have football programs. <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Davis" title="University of California, Davis">UC Davis</a> and <a href="/wiki/California_Polytechnic_State_University" title="California Polytechnic State University">Cal Poly</a> play FCS football in the <a href="/wiki/Big_Sky_Conference" title="Big Sky Conference">Big Sky Conference</a>, and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Hawaii_at_Manoa" title="University of Hawaii at Manoa">Hawai\xca\xbbi</a> <a href="/wiki/Hawaii_Rainbow_Warriors_football" title="Hawaii Rainbow Warriors football">plays FBS football</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Mountain_West_Conference" title="Mountain West Conference">Mountain West Conference</a>.</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Horizon_League" title="Horizon League">Horizon League</a> has one football school in <a href="/wiki/Youngstown_State_University" title="Youngstown State University">Youngstown State</a>, which <a href="/wiki/Youngstown_State_Penguins_football" title="Youngstown State Penguins football">plays</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Missouri_Valley_Football_Conference" title="Missouri Valley Football Conference">Missouri Valley Football Conference</a> (MVFC).</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Metro_Atlantic_Athletic_Conference" title="Metro Atlantic Athletic Conference">Metro Atlantic Athletic Conference</a> (MAAC) has two football schools. <a href="/wiki/Marist_Red_Foxes_football" title="Marist Red Foxes football">Marist</a> plays in the PFL, and <a href="/wiki/Monmouth_Hawks_football" title="Monmouth Hawks football">Monmouth</a> plays in the Big South.</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Missouri_Valley_Conference" title="Missouri Valley Conference">Missouri Valley Conference</a> has seven football schools\xe2\x80\x94<a href="/wiki/Drake_University" title="Drake University">Drake</a>, <a href="/wiki/Illinois_State_University" title="Illinois State University">Illinois State</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indiana_State_University" title="Indiana State University">Indiana State</a>, <a href="/wiki/Missouri_State_University" title="Missouri State University">Missouri State</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Northern_Iowa" title="University of Northern Iowa">Northern Iowa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southern_Illinois_University_Carbondale" title="Southern Illinois University Carbondale">Southern Illinois</a> and <a href="/wiki/Valparaiso_University" title="Valparaiso University">Valparaiso</a>. Drake and Valparaiso play in the PFL, while the others compete in the MVFC (a separate legal entity from the MVC, despite the similar name).</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Summit_League" title="Summit League">The Summit League</a> has five football schools. Four currently play in the MVFC\xe2\x80\x94<a href="/wiki/North_Dakota_State_University" title="North Dakota State University">North Dakota State</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_South_Dakota" title="University of South Dakota">South Dakota</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Dakota_State_University" title="South Dakota State University">South Dakota State</a> and <a href="/wiki/Western_Illinois_University" title="Western Illinois University">Western Illinois</a>. The fifth, 2018 arrival <a href="/wiki/University_of_North_Dakota" title="University of North Dakota">North Dakota</a>, is playing as an FCS independent until joining the MVFC in 2020.</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_Conference" title="West Coast Conference">West Coast Conference</a> has two football schools in <a href="/wiki/Brigham_Young_University" title="Brigham Young University">BYU</a> and <a href="/wiki/University_of_San_Diego" title="University of San Diego">San Diego</a>, which respectively play football as <a href="/wiki/BYU_Cougars_football" title="BYU Cougars football">an FBS independent</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Toreros_football" title="San Diego Toreros football">a PFL member</a>.</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Western_Athletic_Conference" title="Western Athletic Conference">Western Athletic Conference</a> has one football school in <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico_State_University" title="New Mexico State University">New Mexico State</a>, which plays as an FBS independent.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<p>The following Division I conferences do not sponsor <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">football</a>. These conferences still compete in Division I for all sports that they sponsor.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Conferences_4">Conferences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span Division I non-football programs">List of NCAA Division I non-football programs</a></div>\n<dl><dt>Notes</dt></dl>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap mw-references-columns"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-143"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-143">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In addition to the full members, four schools are associate members in a single sport, and a fifth is an associate in two sports.\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Berkeley" title="University of California, Berkeley">California</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_Pacific_(United_States)" title="University of the Pacific (United States)">Pacific</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford</a>, and <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Davis" title="University of California, Davis">UC Davis</a> are associates in field hockey. All will leave the America East in 2019; none has yet announced a future conference affiliation.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Virginia_Military_Institute" title="Virginia Military Institute">VMI</a> is an associate in men\'s and women\'s swimming &amp; diving.</li></ul>\n</span></li>\n<li id="cite_note-144"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-144">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In addition to the full members, the ASUN has four associate members, with one more set to join in the near future:\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Coastal_Carolina_University" title="Coastal Carolina University">Coastal Carolina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mercer_University" title="Mercer University">Mercer</a> compete in beach volleyball.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Kent_State_University" title="Kent State University">Kent State</a>, <a href="/wiki/Howard_University" title="Howard University">Howard</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Old_Dominion_University" title="Old Dominion University">Old Dominion</a> participate only in women\'s lacrosse. <a href="/wiki/University_of_Akron" title="University of Akron">Akron</a> will join this group of schools in 2019.</li></ul>\n</span></li>\n<li id="cite_note-145"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-145">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In addition to the full members, <a href="/wiki/Lock_Haven_University_of_Pennsylvania" title="Lock Haven University of Pennsylvania">Lock Haven</a>, otherwise a Division II institution, and <a href="/wiki/Saint_Francis_University" title="Saint Francis University">Saint Francis (Pennsylvania)</a> are associate members in field hockey.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-146"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-146">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The current Big East was formed in 2013 as a result of <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9313_Big_East_Conference_realignment" title="2010\xe2\x80\x9313 Big East Conference realignment">the split</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Big_East_Conference_(1979%E2%80%932013)" title="Big East Conference (1979\xe2\x80\x932013)">original Big East Conference</a>. The original conference charter was retained by the football-sponsoring schools now known as the <a href="/wiki/American_Athletic_Conference" title="American Athletic Conference">American Athletic Conference</a>. While both leagues claim 1979 as their founding date, the current Big East maintains the history of the original conference in all sports that it sponsors. The pre-split histories of Big East football and rowing\xe2\x80\x94the two sports that are sponsored by The American but not the current Big East\xe2\x80\x94are not recognized by either offshoot conference.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-147"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-147">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In addition to the full members, the following schools are Big East affiliates in one or more sports:\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Connecticut" title="University of Connecticut">Connecticut</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liberty_University" title="Liberty University">Liberty</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quinnipiac_University" title="Quinnipiac University">Quinnipiac</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Temple_University" title="Temple University">Temple</a> participate in field hockey.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Denver" title="University of Denver">Denver</a> participates in men\'s and women\'s lacrosse.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Old_Dominion_University" title="Old Dominion University">Old Dominion</a> participates both in field hockey and women\'s lacrosse.</li></ul>\n</span></li>\n<li id="cite_note-148"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-148">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In addition to the full members, the Big West has three associate members. <a href="/wiki/California_State_University,_Bakersfield" title="California State University, Bakersfield">Cal State Bakersfield</a> and <a href="/wiki/California_State_University,_Sacramento" title="California State University, Sacramento">Sacramento State</a> are members in beach volleyball, and Sacramento State is also a member in men\'s soccer. <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_San_Diego" title="University of California, San Diego">UC San Diego</a>, a Division II member, competes in men\'s volleyball, a sport in which D-I and D-II members compete under identical scholarship limitations for <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Volleyball_Tournament" title="NCAA Men&#39;s Volleyball Tournament">a single national championship</a>. UCSD will add women\'s water polo, a sport with <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Women%27s_Water_Polo_Championship" title="NCAA Women&#39;s Water Polo Championship">a single national championship</a> for all three NCAA divisions, to its Big West membership in 2019.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-149"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-149">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Cal State Bakersfield and UC San Diego will become full members in 2020.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-150"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-150">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Note that "Independents" is not a conference, it is simply a designation used to indicate schools which are not a member of any conference.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-151"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-151">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">There have been no independents since <a href="/wiki/NJIT_Highlanders" title="NJIT Highlanders">New Jersey Institute of Technology</a> joined the Atlantic Sun Conference in 2015.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-152"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-152">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In addition to the full members, 13 other schools are MAAC affiliates in one sport, and three others have multiple sports in the conference.\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/University_at_Albany,_SUNY" title="University at Albany, SUNY">Albany</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Dayton" title="University of Dayton">Dayton</a>, and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Hartford" title="University of Hartford">Hartford</a> participate in women\'s golf.</li>\n<li>Detroit Mercy and <a href="/wiki/St._Bonaventure_University" title="St. Bonaventure University">St. Bonaventure</a> participate in men\'s lacrosse.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Drake_University" title="Drake University">Drake</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Morris_University" title="Robert Morris University">Robert Morris</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Stetson_University" title="Stetson University">Stetson</a> participate in women\'s rowing.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/St._Francis_College" title="St. Francis College">St. Francis Brooklyn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Villanova_University" title="Villanova University">Villanova</a>, <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Military_Institute" title="Virginia Military Institute">VMI</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wagner_College" title="Wagner College">Wagner</a> participate in women\'s water polo.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Bryant_University" title="Bryant University">Bryant</a> participates in field hockey and men\'s swimming and diving.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sacred_Heart_University" title="Sacred Heart University">Sacred Heart</a> participates in field hockey. The MAAC will end sponsorship of field hockey at the end of the 2018 season; the MAAC field hockey conference will be effectively taken over by Sacred Heart\'s full-time home of the Northeast Conference.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_University" title="Jacksonville University">Jacksonville</a> participates in women\'s rowing and the non-NCAA sport of men\'s rowing.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/La_Salle_University" title="La Salle University">La Salle</a> participates in women\'s golf and women\'s water polo.</li></ul>\n</span></li>\n<li id="cite_note-153"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-153">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">22 sports in 2019 with discontinuation of field hockey.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-154"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-154">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In addition to the full members, four schools house one sport in the conference:\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Central_Arkansas" title="University of Central Arkansas">Central Arkansas</a> is an associate in men\'s soccer, but will move that sport to the Sun Belt Conference in 2019.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Dallas_Baptist_University" title="Dallas Baptist University">Dallas Baptist</a>, otherwise a Division II institution, plays baseball.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Arkansas_at_Little_Rock" title="University of Arkansas at Little Rock">Little Rock</a> is an associate in women\'s swimming &amp; diving.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Stony_Brook_University" title="Stony Brook University">Stony Brook</a> competes in women\'s tennis.</li></ul>\n</span></li>\n<li id="cite_note-155"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-155">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In addition to the full members, two schools are single-sport associates, and two others house multiple sports in the conference.\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Drake_University" title="Drake University">Drake</a> and <a href="/wiki/Illinois_State_University" title="Illinois State University">Illinois State</a> are men\'s tennis associates.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Eastern_Illinois_University" title="Eastern Illinois University">Eastern Illinois</a> is an associate member in men\'s soccer, plus men\'s and women\'s swimming &amp; diving.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Valparaiso_University" title="Valparaiso University">Valparaiso</a> is an associate in men\'s swimming (it does not sponsor diving) and men\'s tennis.</li></ul>\n</span></li>\n<li id="cite_note-156"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-156">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In addition to the full members, <a href="/wiki/Creighton_University" title="Creighton University">Creighton</a> is an associate member in women\'s rowing.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-157"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-157">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Cal State Bakersfield will leave for the Big West in 2020.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-158"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-158">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In addition to the full members, the WAC currently has 9 associate members that house one or two sports in the conference:\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/United_States_Air_Force_Academy" title="United States Air Force Academy">Air Force</a> and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Nevada,_Las_Vegas" title="University of Nevada, Las Vegas">UNLV</a> participate in men\'s soccer and men\'s swimming and diving.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Houston_Baptist_University" title="Houston Baptist University">Houston Baptist</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_Incarnate_Word" title="University of the Incarnate Word">Incarnate Word</a>, and <a href="/wiki/San_Jose_State_University" title="San Jose State University">San Jose State</a> participate only in men\'s soccer.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Northern_Colorado" title="University of Northern Colorado">Northern Colorado</a> participates in baseball and women\'s swimming &amp; diving.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Northern_Arizona_University" title="Northern Arizona University">Northern Arizona</a> participates in women\'s swimming and diving.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/California_State_University,_Sacramento" title="California State University, Sacramento">Sacramento State</a> participates in baseball.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Wyoming" title="University of Wyoming">Wyoming</a> participates in men\'s swimming &amp; diving.</li></ul>\n</span></li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<p>Of these, the three that most recently sponsored football were the Atlantic 10, MAAC, and WAC. The A-10 football league dissolved in 2006 with its members going to the Colonial Athletic Association. In addition, four A-10 schools (<a href="/wiki/University_of_Dayton" title="University of Dayton">Dayton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fordham_University" title="Fordham University">Fordham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Duquesne_University" title="Duquesne University">Duquesne</a>, and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Massachusetts_Amherst" title="University of Massachusetts Amherst">Massachusetts</a>) play football in a conference other than the new CAA, which still includes two full-time A-10 members (<a href="/wiki/University_of_Rhode_Island" title="University of Rhode Island">Rhode Island</a> and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Richmond" title="University of Richmond">Richmond</a>). The MAAC stopped sponsoring football in 2007, after most of its members gradually stopped fielding teams. The only pre-2007 MAAC member that still sponsors football is <a href="/wiki/Marist_College" title="Marist College">Marist</a>; <a href="/wiki/Monmouth_University" title="Monmouth University">Monmouth</a> became the second full MAAC member with football upon its arrival in 2013. Marist plays in the Pioneer Football League, while Monmouth spent the 2013 season as an FCS independent before moving its football program into the Big South. The WAC dropped football at the end of the 2012 season, after <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9313_Western_Athletic_Conference_realignment" title="2010\xe2\x80\x9313 Western Athletic Conference realignment">a near-complete membership turnover</a> that saw the conference stripped of all but two of its football-sponsoring members. The two remaining football-sponsoring schools, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Idaho" title="University of Idaho">Idaho</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico_State_University" title="New Mexico State University">New Mexico State</a>, played the 2013 season as FBS independents before becoming football-only members of the Sun Belt Conference in 2014. Both left Sun Belt football in 2018, with Idaho downgrading to FCS status and adding football to its all-sports Big Sky Conference membership and New Mexico State becoming an FBS independent.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Division_I_in_ice_hockey">Division I in ice hockey</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=NCAA_Division_I&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Division I in ice hockey">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Some sports, most notably <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a><sup id="cite_ref-insidecollegehockey.com_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-insidecollegehockey.com-159">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> and men\'s <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">volleyball</a>, have completely different conference structures that operate outside of the normal NCAA sports conference structure.\n</p><p>As <a href="/wiki/College_ice_hockey" title="College ice hockey">ice hockey</a> is limited to a much smaller number of almost exclusively Northern schools, there is a completely different conference structure for teams.<sup id="cite_ref-insidecollegehockey.com_159-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-insidecollegehockey.com-159">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> These conferences feature a mix of teams that play their other sports in various Division I conferences, and even <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_II" title="NCAA Division II">Division II</a> and <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_III" title="NCAA Division III">Division III</a> schools. For most of the early 21st century, there was no correlation between a team\'s ice hockey affiliation and its affiliation for other sports, with the exception of the Ivy League\'s hockey-playing schools all being members of the ECAC. For example, before 2013, the <a href="/wiki/Hockey_East" title="Hockey East">Hockey East</a> men\'s conference consisted of one ACC school, one Big East school, four schools from the America East, one from the A-10, one CAA school, and two schools from the D-II <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Ten_Conference" class="mw-redirect" title="Northeast Ten Conference">Northeast Ten Conference</a>, while the <a href="/wiki/Central_Collegiate_Hockey_Association" title="Central Collegiate Hockey Association">Central Collegiate Hockey Association</a> (CCHA) and <a href="/wiki/Western_Collegiate_Hockey_Association" title="Western Collegiate Hockey Association">Western Collegiate Hockey Association</a> (WCHA) both had some Big Ten representation, plus Division II and III schools. Also, the divisional structure is truncated, with the Division II championship abolished in 1999.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Metro_Atlantic_Athletic_Conference" title="Metro Atlantic Athletic Conference">Metro Atlantic Athletic Conference</a> ceased its sponsorship of the sport in 2003,<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> with the remaining members forming <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Hockey" title="Atlantic Hockey">Atlantic Hockey</a>. For the next decade, no regular all-sport conferences sponsored ice hockey.\n</p><p>Starting with the 2013\xe2\x80\x9314 season, Division I men\'s hockey experienced <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%932014_NCAA_conference_realignment#Hockey" title="2010\xe2\x80\x932014 NCAA conference realignment">a major realignment</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Big_Ten_Conference" title="Big Ten Conference">Big Ten Conference</a> began to sponsor ice hockey, and their institutions withdrew their membership from the WCHA and CCHA.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> Additionally, six other schools from those conferences withdrew to form the new <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Hockey_Conference" title="National Collegiate Hockey Conference">National Collegiate Hockey Conference</a> at the same time.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> The fallout from these moves led to the demise of the CCHA, two more teams entering the NCHC, and further membership turnover in the men\'s side of the WCHA.\n</p><p>Women\'s hockey was largely unaffected by this realignment. The Big Ten still has only four members with varsity women\'s hockey, with six teams required under conference bylaws for official sponsorship. As a result, the only changes in women\'s hockey affiliations in the 2010\xe2\x80\x9314 period occurred in <a href="/wiki/College_Hockey_America" title="College Hockey America">College Hockey America</a>, which saw two schools drop the sport and three new members join.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Conferences_5">Conferences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=NCAA_Division_I&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Conferences">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;e&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>8\n</td>\n<td>8\n</td>\n<td>none\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Western_Collegiate_Hockey_Association"
