lower-alpha;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-163"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-163">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Founded as an all-sports conference in 1896, but did not sponsor ice hockey until 2013\xe2\x80\x9314.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-164"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-164">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Founded as a men\'s-only conference in 1999, with women\'s hockey added in 2002. Men\'s hockey was dropped after the 2009\xe2\x80\x9310 season.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-165"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-165">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The only independent men\'s program in 2018\xe2\x80\x9319 is <a href="/wiki/Arizona_State_Sun_Devils_men%27s_ice_hockey" title="Arizona State Sun Devils men&#39;s ice hockey">Arizona State</a>. Five women\'s programs are currently independent. <a href="/wiki/Sacred_Heart_Pioneers_women%27s_ice_hockey" class="mw-redirect" title="Sacred Heart Pioneers women&#39;s ice hockey">Sacred Heart</a> has played as such since 2003\xe2\x80\x9304, and <a href="/wiki/Franklin_Pierce_Ravens" title="Franklin Pierce Ravens">Franklin Pierce</a>, <a href="/wiki/Post_University" title="Post University">Post</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Anselm_College" title="Saint Anselm College">Saint Anselm</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Saint_Michael%27s_College" title="Saint Michael&#39;s College">Saint Michael\'s</a> began playing as such in 2017\xe2\x80\x9318. All five current independents are part of the New England Women\'s Hockey Alliance, a scheduling agreement that has now organized as a full conference and plans to seek official NCAA recognition for 2019\xe2\x80\x9320 and beyond.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-166"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-166">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">No women\'s independents in 2019 if the NCAA recognizes the NEWHA as a conference. 6 women\'s independents otherwise, with the newly merged LIU athletic program adding the sport in 2019 as a member of the NEWHA.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-167"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-167">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Date of founding; play began in 2013\xe2\x80\x9314.</span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Classification_debate">Classification debate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=NCAA_Division_I&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Classification debate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>In the early 21st century, a controversy arose in the NCAA over whether schools will continue to be allowed to have one showcased program in Division I with the remainder of the athletic program in a lower division, as is the case of, notably, <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_Blue_Jays_men%27s_lacrosse" title="Johns Hopkins Blue Jays men&#39;s lacrosse">Johns Hopkins University lacrosse</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Colorado_College" title="Colorado College">Colorado College</a> and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Alabama_in_Huntsville" title="University of Alabama in Huntsville">University of Alabama in Huntsville</a> in <a href="/wiki/College_ice_hockey" title="College ice hockey">ice hockey</a>. This is an especially important issue in <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">hockey</a>, which has no Division II national championship and has several schools whose other athletic programs compete in Division II and Division III.\n</p><p>This controversy was resolved at the 2004 NCAA Convention in <a href="/wiki/Nashville,_Tennessee" title="Nashville, Tennessee">Nashville, Tennessee</a> when the members supported Proposal 65-1, the amended legislation co-sponsored by <a href="/wiki/Colorado_College" title="Colorado College">Colorado College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clarkson_University" title="Clarkson University">Clarkson University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hartwick_College" title="Hartwick College">Hartwick College</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_University" title="Johns Hopkins University">Johns Hopkins University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rensselaer_Polytechnic_Institute" title="Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute">Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rutgers_University%E2%80%93Newark" title="Rutgers University\xe2\x80\x93Newark">Rutgers University\xe2\x80\x93Newark</a>, <a href="/wiki/St._Lawrence_University" title="St. Lawrence University">St. Lawrence University</a>, and <a href="/wiki/SUNY_Oneonta" class="mw-redirect" title="SUNY Oneonta">SUNY Oneonta</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Each school affected by this debate is allowed to grant financial aid to student-athletes who compete in Division I programs in one men\'s sport and one women\'s sport. It is still permitted for other schools to place one men\'s and one women\'s sport in Division I going forward, but they cannot offer scholarships without bringing the whole program into compliance with Division I rules. In addition, schools in Divisions II and III are allowed to "play up" in any sport that does not have a championship for the school\'s own division, but only Division II programs and any Division III programs covered by the exemption can offer scholarships in those sports.\n</p><p>The Division I programs at each of the eight "waiver schools" which were grandfathered with the passing of Proposal 65-1 were:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Clarkson_University" title="Clarkson University">Clarkson University</a> \xe2\x80\x93 men\'s and women\'s <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Colorado_College" title="Colorado College">Colorado College</a> \xe2\x80\x93 men\'s <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a>, women\'s <a href="/wiki/Soccer" class="mw-redirect" title="Soccer">soccer</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hartwick_College" title="Hartwick College">Hartwick College</a> \xe2\x80\x93 men\'s <a href="/wiki/Soccer" class="mw-redirect" title="Soccer">soccer</a>, women\'s <a href="/wiki/Water_polo" title="Water polo">water polo</a> (men\'s soccer dropped to <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_III" title="NCAA Division III">Division III</a> in 2018, with women\'s water polo discontinued at the same time)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_University" title="Johns Hopkins University">Johns Hopkins University</a> \xe2\x80\x93 men\'s and women\'s <a href="/wiki/Lacrosse" title="Lacrosse">lacrosse</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Rensselaer_Polytechnic_Institute" title="Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute">Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute</a> \xe2\x80\x93 men\'s <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a> (women\'s <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a> moved up to Division I in 2005)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Rutgers_University%E2%80%93Newark" title="Rutgers University\xe2\x80\x93Newark">Rutgers University\xe2\x80\x93Newark</a> \xe2\x80\x93 men\'s <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">volleyball</a> (dropped to Division III in 2014)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/St._Lawrence_University" title="St. Lawrence University">St. Lawrence University</a> \xe2\x80\x93 men\'s and women\'s <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/SUNY_Oneonta" class="mw-redirect" title="SUNY Oneonta">SUNY Oneonta</a> \xe2\x80\x93 men\'s <a href="/wiki/Soccer" class="mw-redirect" title="Soccer">soccer</a> (dropped to Division III in 2006)</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=NCAA_Division_I&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: See
